# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# gRPC Error Status Propagation Across Go Services

## Your Task

Compare how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated in kubernetes/kubernetes vs grafana/grafana vs etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that create gRPC Status errors with codes (codes.NotFound, codes.Internal, etc.) and the files that translate gRPC errors to HTTP responses.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed gRPC error status code handling across the three repositories and created a comprehensive report. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` containing detailed findings about how **kubernetes/kubernetes**, **grafana/grafana**, and **etcd-io/etcd** handle gRPC error status codes:

### Key Findings:

**Kubernetes/Kubernetes:**
- Creates gRPC errors directly with `status.Error(codes.*, message)` in service implementations (CSI mock services)
- Translates to HTTP via two layers: `WriteError()` function and `grpc-gateway`'s `HTTPStatusFromCode()` mapper
- Maps codes like `codes.NotFound` → `http.StatusNotFound`, `codes.ResourceExhausted` → `http.StatusTooManyRequests`

**etcd-io/etcd:**
- Uses centralized error definitions in `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` (70+ predefined gRPC errors)
- Maps internal errors to gRPC errors via `toGRPCErrorMap` and `togRPCError()` function
- Translates to HTTP at multiple layers: interceptors, peer handlers, and HTTP lease handlers
- Falls back to `status.Error(codes.Unknown, err.Error())` for unmapped errors

**Grafana/Grafana:**
- Creates gRPC errors in service handlers (e.g., RBAC service with `codes.NotFound`)
- Translates to backend response codes (not raw HTTP) using `status.FromError()` and code switching
- Has handler functions like `handleGrpcStatusError()` that set error source context (downstream vs plugin)

The report includes 14 relevant files, 13 key symbols, and a narrative explanation of the error propagation patterns and differences between the three projects.

appropriate backend status codes\\n2. **pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go**: The `handleGrpcStatusError()` function sets error source context (ErrorSourceDownstream or translation\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\n**Error Creation Pattern:**\\nGrafana creates gRPC errors in service handlers:\\n- **pkg/services/authz/rbac/service.go**: RBAC service returns Pattern:**\\nGrafana translates gRPC status codes to backend response status codes:\\n1. **pkg/tsdb/influxdb/fsql/fsql.go**: The `Query()` function uses `status.FromError()` to extract gRPC status, then switches on the code (codes.InvalidArgument, codes.PermissionDenied, codes.NotFound, codes.Unavailable, codes.Unauthenticated) to construct `backend.ErrDataResponseWithSource()` responses with appropriate backend status codes\\n2. **pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go**: The `handleGrpcStatusError()` function sets error source context (ErrorSourceDownstream or ErrorSourcePlugin) and returns plugin-specific error wrappers.
